# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Kubernetes Storage Subsystem CSI Driver Integration

## Your Task

Find all Go source files in kubernetes/kubernetes that implement the CSI driver integration: the CSI node plugin client, the CSI volume attach/detach controller, the CSI volume provisioner, and the PersistentVolume controller that bridges CSI operations to the core storage API.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the org domain.

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0, sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0, sg-evals/api--v0.32.0, sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` (etcd-io/etcd)

62-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've created a comprehensive analysis of the CSI driver integration in the kubernetes/kubernetes repository. Here's a summary of what I found:

## CSI Driver Integration Components

I've identified **15 key Go source files** that implement the CSI driver integration:

### Core Components:

1. **CSI Node Plugin Client** (`csi_client.go`) - Implements gRPC communication with CSI drivers for node-level operations (NodePublishVolume, NodeStageVolume, etc.)

2. **CSI Plugin** (`csi_plugin.go`) - Main plugin implementing VolumePlugin, AttachableVolumePlugin, and BlockVolumePlugin interfaces. Handles CSI driver registration and plugin initialization.

3. **CSI Volume Attacher** (`csi_attacher.go`) - Implements Attach/Detach operations, coordinating with the attach/detach controller via VolumeAttachment objects.

4. **CSI Mount Manager** (`csi_mounter.go`) - Handles volume mounting/unmounting by calling CSI node plugin methods.

5. **CSI Block Mapper** (`csi_block.go`) - Manages block-level volume operations.

6. **Attach/Detach Controller** (`attach_detach_controller.go`) - Cluster-level controller managing volume attachment state and reconciliation.

7. **PersistentVolume Controller** (`pv_controller.go`, `pv_controller_base.go`) - Bridges CSI operations to the core storage API, handling dynamic provisioning and volume lifecycle management.

8. **CSI Node Info Manager** (`nodeinfomanager.go`) - Manages CSI driver registration on nodes and CSINode object lifecycle.

9. **CSI Node Updater** (`csi_node_updater.go`) - Dynamically updates node allocatable information.

The complete analysis with all files, symbols, and the interaction chain has been saved to `/workspace/answer.json`.

None of the versions specified %q are supported. err=%v\\\", callerName, pluginName, versions, err))\\n256: \\t}\\n257: \\n258: \\texistingDriver, driverExists := csiDrivers.Get(pluginName)\\n259: \\tif driverExists {\\n260: \\t\\tif !existingDriver.highestSupportedVersion.LessThan(newDriverHighestVersion) {\\n261: \\t\\t\\treturn nil, errors.New(log(\\\"%s for CSI driver %q failed. Another driver with the same name is already registered with a higher supported version: %q\\\", callerName, pluginName, existingDriver.highestSupportedVersion))\\n262: \\t\\t}\\n263: \\t}\\n264: \\n265: \\treturn newDriverHighestVersion, nil\\n266: }\\n267: \\n268: // DeRegisterPlugin is called when a plugin removed its socket, signaling\\n269: // it is no longer available\\n270: func (h validateVersions(callerName, pluginName string, endpoint string, versions []string) (*utilversion.Version, error) {\n243: \tif len(versions) == 0 {\n244: \t\treturn nil, errors.New(log(\"%s for CSI driver %q failed. Plugin returned an empty list for supported versions\", callerName, pluginName))\n245: \t}\n246: \n247: \t// Validate version\n248: \t// CSI currently only has version 0.x and 1.x (see https://github.com/container-storage-interface/spec/releases).\n249: \t// Therefore any driver claiming version 2.x+ is ignored as an unsupported versions.\n250: \t// Future 1.x versions of CSI are supposed to be backwards compatible so this version of Kubernetes will work with any 1.x driver\n251: \t// (or 0.x), but it may not work with 2.x drivers (because 2.x does not have to be backwards compatible with 1.x).\n252: \t// CSI v0.x is no longer supported as of Kubernetes v1.17 in accordance with deprecation policy set out in Kubernetes v1.13.\n253: \tnewDriverHighestVersion, err := utilversion.HighestSupportedVersion(versions)\n254: \tif err != nil {\n255: \t\treturn nil, errors.New(log(\"%s for CSI driver %q failed. None of the versions specified %q are supported. err=%v\", callerName, pluginName, versions, err))\n256: \t}\n257: \n258: \texistingDriver, driverExists := csiDrivers.Get(pluginName)\n259: \tif driverExists {\n260: \t\tif !existingDriver.highestSupportedVersion.LessThan(newDriverHighestVersion) {\n261: \t\t\treturn nil, errors.New(log(\"%s for CSI driver %q failed. Another driver with the same name is already registered with a higher supported version: %q\", callerName, pluginName, existingDriver.highestSupportedVersion))\n262: \t\t}\n263: \t}\n264: \n265: \treturn newDriverHighestVersion, nil\n266: }\n267: \n268: // DeRegisterPlugin is called when a plugin removed its socket, signaling\n269: // it is no longer available\n270: func (h \t\t\tklog.Fatalf(\"Failed to initialize CSINode after retrying: %v\", err)\n414: \t\t}\n415: \t}()\n416: \n417: \tif utilfeature.DefaultFeatureGate.Enabled(features.MutableCSINodeAllocatableCount) &&
